	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">KFC</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the fast food chicken restaurant chain. <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar"><span style="word-spacing:0">This box: </span><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Infobox_KFC" title="Template:Infobox KFC"><span title="View this template">view</span></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Infobox_KFC" title="Template talk:Infobox KFC"><span title="Discuss this template">talk</span></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Infobox_KFC&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template">edit</span></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>KFC</b>, also known as <b>Kentucky Fried Chicken</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> is an American <a href="/wiki/Fast_food_restaurant" title="Fast food restaurant">fast food restaurant</a> chain headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville, Kentucky</a>, that specializes in <a href="/wiki/Fried_chicken" title="Fried chicken">fried chicken</a>. It is the world's second-largest restaurant chain (as measured by sales) after <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a>, with 22,621 locations globally in 136 countries as of December 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=KFC&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The chain is a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Yum!_Brands" title="Yum! Brands">Yum! Brands</a>, a restaurant company that also owns the <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taco_Bell" title="Taco Bell">Taco Bell</a> and <a href="/wiki/WingStreet" title="WingStreet">WingStreet</a> chains.<sup id="cite_ref-YUM!-Brands-Feb-2018-10-K_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YUM!-Brands-Feb-2018-10-K-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg/220px-KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg/330px-KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg/440px-KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2965" data-file-height="1919" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Hot_Wings_Fries.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KFC Hot Wings and fries</div></div></div>
<p>KFC was founded by <a href="/wiki/Colonel_Sanders" title="Colonel Sanders">Colonel Harland Sanders</a>, an entrepreneur who began selling fried chicken from his roadside restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Corbin,_Kentucky" title="Corbin, Kentucky">Corbin, Kentucky</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. Sanders identified the potential of the restaurant <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchising</a> concept, and the first "Kentucky Fried Chicken" franchise opened in <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> in 1952. KFC popularized chicken in the fast food industry, diversifying the market by challenging the established dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Hamburger" title="Hamburger">hamburger</a>. By branding himself as "Colonel Sanders", Harland became a prominent figure of American cultural history, and his image remains widely used in KFC advertising to this day. However, the company's rapid expansion overwhelmed the aging Sanders, and he sold it to a group of investors led by <a href="/wiki/John_Y._Brown_Jr." title="John Y. Brown Jr.">John Y. Brown Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_C._Massey" title="Jack C. Massey">Jack C. Massey</a> in 1964.
</p><p>KFC was one of the first American fast food chains to expand internationally, opening outlets in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> by the mid-1960s. Throughout the 1970s and 1980s, it experienced mixed fortunes domestically, as it went through a series of changes in corporate ownership with little or no experience in the restaurant business. In the early 1970s, KFC was sold to the <a href="/wiki/Distilled_spirit" class="mw-redirect" title="Distilled spirit">spirits</a> distributor <a href="/wiki/Heublein" title="Heublein">Heublein</a>, which was taken over by the <a href="/wiki/R._J._Reynolds_Tobacco_Company" title="R. J. Reynolds Tobacco Company">R.J. Reynolds</a> food and <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> conglomerate; that company sold the chain to <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a>. The chain continued to expand overseas, however, and in 1987, it became the first Western restaurant chain to open in China. It has since expanded rapidly in China, which is now the company's single largest market. PepsiCo <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">spun off</a> its restaurants division as Tricon Global Restaurants, which later changed its name to Yum! Brands.
</p><p>KFC's original product is <a href="/wiki/Pressure_frying" title="Pressure frying">pressure-fried</a> chicken pieces, seasoned with Sanders' recipe of 11 herbs and spices. The constituents of the recipe represent a notable <a href="/wiki/Trade_secret" title="Trade secret">trade secret</a>. Larger portions of fried chicken are served in a cardboard "bucket", which has become a well-known feature of the chain since it was first introduced by franchisee <a href="/wiki/Pete_Harman" title="Pete Harman">Pete Harman</a> in 1957. Since the early 1990s, KFC has expanded its menu to offer other chicken products such as <a href="/wiki/Chicken_sandwich" title="Chicken sandwich">chicken fillet sandwiches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrap_(sandwich)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wrap (sandwich)">wraps</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Side_dish" title="Side dish">side dishes</a> such as <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">French fries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coleslaw" title="Coleslaw">coleslaw</a>, desserts, and <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a>; the latter often supplied by <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a>. KFC is known for its <a href="/wiki/Slogan" title="Slogan">slogans</a> "It's Finger Lickin' Good!", "Nobody does chicken like KFC" and "So good".
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_KFC" title="History of KFC">History of KFC</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png/280px-Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png/420px-Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png/560px-Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="233" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Col_Sanders_Restaurant.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Harland_Sanders_Caf%C3%A9_and_Museum" title="Harland Sanders Café and Museum">Harland Sanders Café and Museum</a> in Corbin, Kentucky</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Colonel_Sanders" title="Colonel Sanders">Harland Sanders</a> was born in 1890 and raised on a farm outside <a href="/wiki/Henryville,_Indiana" title="Henryville, Indiana">Henryville, Indiana</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville, Kentucky</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated44_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated44-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> When Sanders was five years old, his father died, forcing his mother to work at a <a href="/wiki/Canning" title="Canning">canning</a> plant.<sup id="cite_ref-Klotter2005_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Klotter2005-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> This left Sanders, as the eldest son, to care for his two younger siblings.<sup id="cite_ref-Klotter2005_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Klotter2005-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> After he reached seven years of age, his mother taught him how to cook.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated44_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated44-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> After leaving the family home at the age of 13, Sanders passed through several professions, with mixed success.<sup id="cite_ref-celebritychef3_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-celebritychef3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1930, he took over a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Shell</a> <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">filling station</a> on <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_25_in_Kentucky" title="U.S. Route 25 in Kentucky">US Route 25</a> just outside <a href="/wiki/North_Corbin,_Kentucky" title="North Corbin, Kentucky">North Corbin, Kentucky</a>, a small town on the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ozersky2012_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ozersky2012-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It was here that he first served to travelers the recipes that he had learned as a child: fried chicken and other dishes such as steaks and <a href="/wiki/Country_ham" title="Country ham">country ham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ozersky2012_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ozersky2012-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> After four years of serving from his own dining room table, Sanders purchased the larger filling station on the other side of the road and expanded to six tables.<sup id="cite_ref-Aaseng2001_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aaseng2001-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> By 1936, this had proven successful enough for Sanders to be given the honorary title of <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_colonel" class="mw-redirect" title="Kentucky colonel">Kentucky colonel</a> by <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Kentucky" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors of Kentucky">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Ruby_Laffoon" title="Ruby Laffoon">Ruby Laffoon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith2011_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2011-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In 1937 he expanded his restaurant to 142 seats, and added a <a href="/wiki/Motel" title="Motel">motel</a> he purchased across the street, naming it <a href="/wiki/Harland_Sanders_Caf%C3%A9_and_Museum" title="Harland Sanders Café and Museum">Sanders Court &amp; Café</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hollis1920_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollis1920-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sanders was unhappy with the 35 minutes it took to prepare his chicken in an iron frying pan, but he refused to <a href="/wiki/Deep_fry" class="mw-redirect" title="Deep fry">deep fry</a> the chicken, which he believed lowered the quality of the product.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated52_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated52-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> If he pre-cooked the chicken in advance of orders, there was sometimes wastage at day's end.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated44_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated44-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 1939, the first commercial <a href="/wiki/Pressure_cooker" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressure cooker">pressure cookers</a> were released onto the market, mostly designed for steaming vegetables.<sup id="cite_ref-Binney2012_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Binney2012-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Sanders bought one, and modified it into a <a href="/wiki/Pressure_fryer" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressure fryer">pressure fryer</a>, which he then used to fry chicken.<sup id="cite_ref-history_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The new method reduced production time to be comparable with deep frying, while, in the opinion of Sanders, retaining the quality of pan-fried chicken.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated52_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated52-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 1940, Sanders finalised what came to be known as his "Original Recipe" of 11 herbs and spices.<sup id="cite_ref-july1940_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-july1940-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Although he never publicly revealed the recipe, he admitted to the use of salt and pepper, and claimed that the ingredients "stand on everybody's shelf".<sup id="cite_ref-Kleber1992_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kleber1992-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> After being recommissioned as a Kentucky colonel in 1950 by Governor <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Wetherby" title="Lawrence Wetherby">Lawrence Wetherby</a>, Sanders began to dress the part, growing a <a href="/wiki/Goatee" title="Goatee">goatee</a> and wearing a black <a href="/wiki/Frock_coat" title="Frock coat">frock coat</a> (later switched to a white suit), a <a href="/wiki/String_tie" class="mw-redirect" title="String tie">string tie</a>, and referring to himself as "Colonel".<sup id="cite_ref-Kleber1992_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kleber1992-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> His associates went along with the title change, "jokingly at first and then in earnest", according to biographer <a href="/wiki/Josh_Ozersky" class="mw-redirect" title="Josh Ozersky">Josh Ozersky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ozersky_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ozersky-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg/170px-Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg/255px-Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg/340px-Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg 2x" data-file-width="503" data-file-height="679" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colonel_Harland_Sanders_in_character.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harland Sanders in character as "The Colonel"</div></div></div>
<p>The Sanders Court &amp; Café generally served travelers, so when the route planned in 1955 for <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75" title="Interstate 75">Interstate 75</a> bypassed <a href="/wiki/Corbin,_Kentucky" title="Corbin, Kentucky">Corbin</a>, Sanders sold his properties and traveled the US to franchise his chicken recipe to restaurant owners.<sup id="cite_ref-JakleSculle1999_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JakleSculle1999-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Independent restaurants would pay four (later five) <a href="/wiki/Cent_(currency)" title="Cent (currency)">cents</a> on each chicken as a franchise fee, in exchange for Sanders' "secret blend of herbs and spices" and the right to feature his recipe on their menus and use his name and likeness for promotional purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated15_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1952 he had already successfully franchised his recipe to his friend <a href="/wiki/Pete_Harman" title="Pete Harman">Pete Harman</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Salt_Lake,_Utah" title="South Salt Lake, Utah">South Salt Lake, Utah</a>, the operator of one of the city's largest restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-mashed_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mashed-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Don Anderson, a sign painter hired by Harman, coined the name "Kentucky Fried Chicken".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated26_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated26-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> For Harman, the addition of KFC was a way of differentiating his restaurant from competitors; a product from Kentucky was exotic, and evoked imagery of <a href="/wiki/Southern_hospitality" title="Southern hospitality">Southern hospitality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated26_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated26-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Harman trademarked the phrase "It's finger lickin' good", which eventually became the company-wide slogan.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated15_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He also introduced the "bucket meal" in 1957 (14 pieces of chicken, five <a href="/wiki/Bread_roll" title="Bread roll">bread rolls</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Pint" title="Pint">pint</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gravy" title="Gravy">gravy</a> in a cardboard bucket).<sup id="cite_ref-Darden1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darden1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Serving their signature meal in a paper bucket was to become an iconic feature of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Darden1_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darden1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1963 there were 600 KFC restaurants, making the company the largest fast food operation in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-JakleSculle1999_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JakleSculle1999-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> KFC popularized chicken in the fast food industry, diversifying the market by challenging the established dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Hamburger" title="Hamburger">hamburger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith2007_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2007-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1964, Sanders sold the company to a group of investors led by <a href="/wiki/John_Y._Brown_Jr." title="John Y. Brown Jr.">John Y. Brown Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_C._Massey" title="Jack C. Massey">Jack C. Massey</a> for US$2 million (around US$15 million in 2013).<sup id="cite_ref-Smith2011_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2011-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The contract included a lifetime salary for Sanders and the agreement that he would be the company's quality controller and trademark.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoFE-5_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoFE-5-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The chain had reached 3,000 outlets in 48 different countries by 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated40_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated40-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In July 1971, Brown sold the company to the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Heublein" title="Heublein">Heublein</a>, a packaged food and drinks corporation, for US$285 million (around US$1.6 billion in 2013).<sup id="cite_ref-AutoFE-10_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoFE-10-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Sanders died in 1980, his promotional work making him a prominent figure in American cultural history.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith2007_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2007-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> By the time of his death, there were an estimated 6,000 KFC outlets in 48 different countries worldwide, with $2 billion of sales annually.<sup id="cite_ref-washpostobit_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washpostobit-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1982, Heublein was acquired by <a href="/wiki/R._J._Reynolds" title="R. J. Reynolds">R. J. Reynolds</a>, the tobacco giant.<sup id="cite_ref-Darden1_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darden1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In July 1986, Reynolds sold KFC to <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a> for $850 million (around US$1.8 billion in 2013).<sup id="cite_ref-AutoFE-15_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoFE-15-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> PepsiCo made the chain a part of its restaurants division alongside <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taco_Bell" title="Taco Bell">Taco Bell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The Chinese market was entered in November 1987, with an outlet in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Darden1_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darden1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991, the KFC name was officially adopted, although it was already widely known by that <a href="/wiki/Initialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Initialism">initialism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Kyle Craig, president of KFC US, admitted the change was an attempt to distance the chain from the unhealthy connotations of "fried".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The early 1990s saw a number of successful major products launched throughout the chain, including spicy "Hot Wings" (launched in 1990), popcorn chicken (1992), and internationally, the "Zinger", a spicy chicken fillet sandwich (1993).<sup id="cite_ref-newitems_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newitems-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> By 1994, KFC had 5,149 outlets in the US, and 9,407 overall, with over 100,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated31_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated31-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In August 1997, PepsiCo spun off its restaurants division as a public company valued at US$4.5 billion (around US$6.5 billion in 2013).<sup id="cite_ref-AutoFE-19_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoFE-19-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The new company was named <a href="/wiki/Tricon_Global_Restaurants" class="mw-redirect" title="Tricon Global Restaurants">Tricon Global Restaurants</a>, and at the time had 30,000 outlets and annual sales of US$10 billion (around US$14 billion in 2013), making it second in the world only to McDonald's.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoFE-21_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoFE-21-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Tricon was renamed <a href="/wiki/Yum!_Brands" title="Yum! Brands">Yum! Brands</a> in May 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-tricontoyum_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tricontoyum-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2015, the company was struggling, having lost business to other retailers and being surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Chick-fil-A" title="Chick-fil-A">Chick-fil-A</a> as the leading chicken retailer in the U.S. three years previously. To combat this, the company launched a new initiative with a plan to revamp its packaging, decor and uniforms, as well as expanding its menu. Additionally, beginning in May 2015, a new series of advertisements was launched featuring <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Hammond" title="Darrell Hammond">Darrell Hammond</a> as Colonel Sanders.<sup id="cite_ref-2015revamp_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015revamp-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently,  in a planned rotation of actors, <a href="/wiki/Norm_Macdonald" title="Norm Macdonald">Norm Macdonald</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Gaffigan" title="Jim Gaffigan">Jim Gaffigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton_(actor)" title="George Hamilton (actor)">George Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Riggle" title="Rob Riggle">Rob Riggle</a> portrayed Sanders in similar ads through the fall of 2016. In January 2018, Country Music icon <a href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire" title="Reba McEntire">Reba McEntire</a> was chosen to be KFC's first female Colonel Sanders.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_with_KFC_franchises" title="List of countries with KFC franchises">List of countries with KFC franchises</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_world_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/KFC_world_map.svg/220px-KFC_world_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/KFC_world_map.svg/330px-KFC_world_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/KFC_world_map.svg/440px-KFC_world_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1134" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_world_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of countries with KFC franchises as of September 2018</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Home_Base.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/KFC_Home_Base.jpg/220px-KFC_Home_Base.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/KFC_Home_Base.jpg/330px-KFC_Home_Base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/KFC_Home_Base.jpg/440px-KFC_Home_Base.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="978" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Home_Base.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A stand-alone KFC <a href="/wiki/Drive-through" title="Drive-through">drive-through</a> unit located in Australia</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_(Quito,_Ecuador).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_%28Quito%2C_Ecuador%29.png/220px-KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_%28Quito%2C_Ecuador%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_%28Quito%2C_Ecuador%29.png/330px-KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_%28Quito%2C_Ecuador%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_%28Quito%2C_Ecuador%29.png/440px-KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_%28Quito%2C_Ecuador%29.png 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="519" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Cumbay%C3%A1_(Quito,_Ecuador).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A KFC outlet in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>; the largest market for the chain in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Qatar,_Al_Khor_(24),_KFC.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Qatar%2C_Al_Khor_%2824%29%2C_KFC.JPG/220px-Qatar%2C_Al_Khor_%2824%29%2C_KFC.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Qatar%2C_Al_Khor_%2824%29%2C_KFC.JPG/330px-Qatar%2C_Al_Khor_%2824%29%2C_KFC.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Qatar%2C_Al_Khor_%2824%29%2C_KFC.JPG/440px-Qatar%2C_Al_Khor_%2824%29%2C_KFC.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Qatar,_Al_Khor_(24),_KFC.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A KFC restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Al_Khor_(city)" title="Al Khor (city)">Al Khor</a>, rural Qatar</div></div></div>
<p>KFC is a subsidiary of Yum! Brands, one of the largest restaurant companies in the world. KFC had sales of $23 billion in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-yumpresentation_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yumpresentation-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> KFC has its headquarters at 1441 Gardiner Lane, <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville, Kentucky</a>, in a three-story <a href="/wiki/Colonial_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial style">colonial style</a> building known colloquially as the "White House" due to its resemblance to the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">US president's home</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kleber2000_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kleber2000-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-storey_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-storey-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The headquarters contain executive offices and the company's <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated51_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated51-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> KFC is <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> at <a href="/wiki/Corporation_Trust_Center_(CT_Corporation)" title="Corporation Trust Center (CT Corporation)">1209 North Orange St</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">Wilmington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thimmesch_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thimmesch-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC,_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/KFC%2C_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg/220px-KFC%2C_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/KFC%2C_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg/330px-KFC%2C_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/KFC%2C_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg/440px-KFC%2C_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg 2x" data-file-width="2256" data-file-height="1504" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC,_along_with_various_other_stores_on_Hong_Kong_Island..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KFC <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Island" title="Hong Kong Island">Hong Kong Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>By December 2013, there were 18,875 KFC outlets in 118 countries and territories around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-restcount_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-restcount-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> There are 4,563 outlets in China, 4,491 in the United States, and 9,821 across the rest of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-restcount_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-restcount-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Outlets are owned by franchisees or directly by the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Jing1_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jing1-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Eleven percent of outlets are company owned, with the rest operated by franchise holders.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Capital_intensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital intensive">capital intensive</a>, company ownership allows for faster expansion of the chain.<sup id="cite_ref-steyn_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steyn-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most restaurants are furnished with images of the company founder, Colonel Harland Sanders.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated51_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated51-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> As well as dine-in and take-out, many stand-alone KFC outlets offer a <a href="/wiki/Drive-through" title="Drive-through">drive-through</a> option.<sup id="cite_ref-Cartwright2003_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cartwright2003-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> KFC offers a limited delivery service in a small number of markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Cartwright2003_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cartwright2003-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Units include express concessions and <a href="/wiki/Kiosks" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiosks">kiosks</a> which feature a limited menu and operated in non-traditional locations such as filling stations, <a href="/wiki/Convenience_store" title="Convenience store">convenience stores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stadium" title="Stadium">stadia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theme_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Theme park">theme parks</a> and <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">colleges</a>, where a full scale outlet would not be practical.<sup id="cite_ref-Cartwright2003_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cartwright2003-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Average annual sales per unit was $1.2 million in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-novakpres_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-novakpres-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Worldwide, the daily average number of food orders at an outlet is 250, with most occurring within a two-hour peak-period.<sup id="cite_ref-Balakrishnan132_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balakrishnan132-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a Director and CEO of Yum!, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Creed" title="Greg Creed">Greg Creed</a><sup id="cite_ref-ceos_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceos-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> ultimately has foremost responsibility for KFC operations. Sam Su is chairman and CEO of Yum!'s Chinese operations, and Tony Lowings is the president and CEO of KFC, replacing <a href="/wiki/Roger_Eaton" title="Roger Eaton">Roger Eaton</a> who retired in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> David Gibbs is president, CFO and COO of Yum! Brands, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-ceos_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceos-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> On March 7, 2019 KFC announced a new executive position <a href="/wiki/Chief_communications_officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief communications officer">"Chief Communications Officer"</a> and Staci Rawls will fill that position.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC,_Ilorin.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/KFC%2C_Ilorin.JPG/220px-KFC%2C_Ilorin.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/KFC%2C_Ilorin.JPG/330px-KFC%2C_Ilorin.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/KFC%2C_Ilorin.JPG/440px-KFC%2C_Ilorin.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1412" data-file-height="1059" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC,_Ilorin.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KFC restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Ilorin" title="Ilorin">Ilorin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwara_State" title="Kwara State">Kwara</a>, Nigeria</div></div></div>
<p>The company hopes to expand its African operations, where it is already the regional leader among US fast food chains.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The company is slowly expanding across the African continent, opening 70 outlets, but progress has been hampered by sourcing issues, such as a lack of quality suppliers.<sup id="cite_ref-steyn_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steyn-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span></h3>
<p>KFC continues to grow in Asia.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, KFC was launched in 1995 at <a href="/wiki/Majestic_City" title="Majestic City">Majestic City</a>. There were 25 KFC restaurants in Sri Lanka as of December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, the first KFC franchise was opened in 1977 along Somerset Road. In 1993, KFC Singapore was the first KFC in Asia to develop and launch the Zinger. KFC restaurants in Singapore are currently owned and operated by KFC (Malaysia) Holdings Bhd.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, the first KFC outlet was opened at <a href="/wiki/Gulshan,_Dhaka" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulshan, Dhaka">Gulshan</a> in 2006. As of June 2016, the country is home to 19 KFC outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, KFC first opened on <a href="/wiki/Monivong_Boulevard" title="Monivong Boulevard">Monivong Boulevard</a> in <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, the first KFC outlet was officially opened on <a href="/wiki/Bogyoke_Aung_San_Road" title="Bogyoke Aung San Road">Bogyoke Aung San Road</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yangon" title="Yangon">Yangon</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, KFC has a presence in eighteen major cities of Pakistan (Karachi, Lahore, Islamabad, Rawalpindi, Gujranwala, Sukkur, Muree etc.) with more than 65 outlets nationwide. Its first outlet was in Gulshan-e-Iqbal, Karachi. KFC Pakistan menu consists of sandwiches, fried chicken, nuggets, fries, rice dishes and drinks.<sup id="cite_ref-about_us_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about_us-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, KFC entered the market in 1984 and opened its first store in 1985 in <a href="/wiki/Taipei_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Taipei City">Taipei City</a>. The 100th store in Taiwan opened in 1999. It was the second largest fast food chain restaurant in Taiwan until <a href="/wiki/Mos_Burger" class="mw-redirect" title="Mos Burger">Mos Burger</a> exceeded the number of branches of KFC in 2008. Now KFC is the third largest fast food chain restaurant with 137 stores as of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/KFC_in_China" title="KFC in China">KFC in China</a></div>
<p>KFC is the largest restaurant chain in China, with 5,003 outlets as of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Yum!-Brands-AR2015_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yum!-Brands-AR2015-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> They are operated by the Yum! China division. KFC became the first Western fast food company in China after its first outlet opened in <a href="/wiki/Qianmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Qianmen">Qianmen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, in November 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Local food items include rice <a href="/wiki/Congee" title="Congee">congee</a> and tree fungus salad, with an average of 50 different menu items per store.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shen_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shen-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2012, the chain faced allegations that some of its suppliers injected <a href="/wiki/Antiviral_drug" title="Antiviral drug">antiviral drugs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Growth_hormone" title="Growth hormone">growth hormones</a> into poultry in ways that violated food safety regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> This resulted in the chain severing its relationship with 100 suppliers, and agreeing to "actively co-operate" with a government investigation into its use of antibiotics.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> KFC China sales in January 2013 were down 41 percent against the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated41_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated41-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> To counter sluggish sales, the menu was revamped in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-revampchina_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revampchina-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2014, Chinese authorities closed down the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> operations of the <a href="/wiki/OSI_Group" title="OSI Group">OSI Group</a>, amidst allegations that it had supplied KFC with expired meat.<sup id="cite_ref-2014chinasafety_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014chinasafety-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Yum! immediately terminated its contract with the supplier, and stated that the revelation had led to a "significant [and] negative" decline in sales.<sup id="cite_ref-yumresponse14_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yumresponse14-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KFC opens its first outlet in <a href="/wiki/Tibet_Autonomous_Region" title="Tibet Autonomous Region">Tibet</a> in March 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg/220px-Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg/330px-Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg/440px-Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1025" data-file-height="869" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kolkata_Choweinghee_6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KFC outlet on Middleton Row in <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Polayathode,_Kollam_city.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/KFC_Polayathode%2C_Kollam_city.jpg/220px-KFC_Polayathode%2C_Kollam_city.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/KFC_Polayathode%2C_Kollam_city.jpg/330px-KFC_Polayathode%2C_Kollam_city.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/KFC_Polayathode%2C_Kollam_city.jpg/440px-KFC_Polayathode%2C_Kollam_city.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Polayathode,_Kollam_city.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KFC in <a href="/wiki/Polayathode" title="Polayathode">Polayathode</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kollam" title="Kollam">Kollam</a> city. This is one of the largest KFC stores in <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a> state</div></div></div>
<p>There are 350 KFC outlets in India.<sup id="cite_ref-Yum!-Brands-AR2015_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yum!-Brands-AR2015-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>  The company has adapted the standard KFC offerings to Indian tastes<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and the menu options in India include the Hot &amp; Crispy Chicken and Fiery Grilled bucket options, Chicken Zinger, Krushers, Rice Bowlz and the more recently launched 5-in-1 Meal Box.<sup id="cite_ref-India_Infoline_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India_Infoline-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The business was refranchised in October 2015 after Yum concluded a year-and-a-half-long exercise to reorganize its business under larger, well-capitalized franchisees. In this regard, about a third of its outlets, operated by several of its franchisees, have been sold to a newly formed entity—Sapphire Foods India Pvt. Ltd. The new entity is owned by a consortium of four private equity funds, led by Samara Capital. The other investors are CX Partners, Goldman Sachs Group Inc. and a fourth fund, said a top executive at the local arm of the American food company.<sup id="cite_ref-Live_Mint_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Live_Mint-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first Indian KFC was a two-storey outlet on the fashionable <a href="/wiki/Brigade_Road" title="Brigade Road">Brigade Road</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a> in June 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-TichyMcGill1997_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TichyMcGill1997-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> According to journalist <a href="/wiki/Michael_White_(journalist)" title="Michael White (journalist)">Michael White</a>, the company could not have chosen a "more difficult venue for its maiden entrée into the country".<sup id="cite_ref-White2009_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White2009-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Bangalore housed the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Karnataka_Rajya_Raitha_Sangha" title="Karnataka Rajya Raitha Sangha">Karnataka Rajya Raitha Sangha</a>, one of the most influential, vocal and anti-foreign investment farmers' associations in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-White2009_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White2009-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The first outlet suffered protests from <a href="/wiki/Anti-globalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-globalisation">anti-globalisation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">environmental</a> campaigners, as well as local farmers, who objected to the chain bypassing local producers.<sup id="cite_ref-BergerHuntington2003_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BergerHuntington2003-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Many<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (September 2015)">quantify</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Indians were concerned about the onslaught of <a href="/wiki/Consumerism" title="Consumerism">consumerism</a>, the loss of national self-sufficiency, and the disruption of indigenous traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Derné2008_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Derné2008-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The protests came to a head in August 1995, when the Bangalore outlet was repeatedly ransacked.<sup id="cite_ref-TichyMcGill1997_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TichyMcGill1997-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The KFC outlet in Bangalore demanded, and received, a police van permanently parked outside for a year.<sup id="cite_ref-BergerHuntington2003_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BergerHuntington2003-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The outlet was closed on September 13, 1995 by local authorities, who claimed the company used illegally high amounts of <a href="/wiki/Monosodium_glutamate" title="Monosodium glutamate">monosodium glutamate</a> (MSG) in its food.<sup id="cite_ref-Dayal-GulatiJain2010_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dayal-GulatiJain2010-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The outlet re-opened a few hours later as the result of an appeal by KFC to the <a href="/wiki/Karnataka_High_Court" title="Karnataka High Court">Karnataka High Court</a>. The company stated the recipe was no different than that used in any other KFC store.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Rural activist <a href="/wiki/M._D._Nanjundaswamy" title="M. D. Nanjundaswamy">M. D. Nanjundaswamy</a> claimed KFC would adversely affect the health of the impoverished, by diverting grain from poor people to make the more profitable animal feed.<sup id="cite_ref-Gupta1998_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta1998-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Environmentalist <a href="/wiki/Maneka_Gandhi" title="Maneka Gandhi">Maneka Gandhi</a> joined the anti-KFC movement.<sup id="cite_ref-Gupta1998_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta1998-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> A second outlet opened in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, but was closed by the authorities throughout November, purportedly for health reasons, but more likely to avoid a repetition of the Bangalore incident.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The Delhi outlet soon closed permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-amrit_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amrit-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KFC began to expand outside of Bangalore in 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-tandoori_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tandoori-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> with a localized menu that was the most extensive meat-free menu across the chain's worldwide operations. It introduced a vegetarian menu that included rice meals, wraps and side dishes and, like McDonald's, served eggless mayonnaise and sauces. Unnat Varma, marketing director of KFC India, states "The vegetarian offerings have made the brand more relevant to a larger section of consumers and that is necessary for KFC's growth." KFC also began using Indian spices and cooking techniques to localize its chicken dishes. By 2008–09, KFC operated 34 outlets in India.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, KFC launched the "So Veg, So Good" menu as part of an India-specific promotional strategy focused on enhancing their vegetarian range. The company has been up to a lot of innovation over the past few months with the launch of the first-ever no crust, all chicken KFC Chizza in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-IIFL_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IIFL-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>  More recently, KFC got <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dabbawala" title="Dabbawala">dabbawalas</a> to deliver its newly launched 5-in-1 Meal Boxes. The city's dabbawalas, famed for their efficient delivery of office lunches, took on the role of KFC delivery men as part of an innovative marketing campaign. They supplied specially created 5-in-1 meal boxes to some office-goers instead of their regular dabbas.<sup id="cite_ref-India_Today_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India_Today-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The innovation efforts have continued with the launch of the Watt a Box, a practical new take on the 5-in-1 Meal Box, which can also charge phones.<sup id="cite_ref-TIME_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIME-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg/220px-KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg/330px-KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg/440px-KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="531" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Bandung_Supermall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A counter at a KFC in <a href="/wiki/Bandung" title="Bandung">Bandung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, KFC is the largest Western restaurant chain, with 466 outlets as of December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-restcount_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-restcount-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rappeport_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rappeport-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The chain has grown to hold an estimated 32 percent market share, and menu items include spaghetti, wraps and chicken porridge.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The master franchisee is PT Fastfood Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated45_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated45-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first outlet opened in Jakarta in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated45_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated45-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Salim_Group" title="Salim Group">Salim Group</a>, Indonesia's largest conglomerate, became a major shareholder in 1990, which provided the company with funds for major expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated45_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated45-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Its master franchisee, PT Fastfood Indonesia, was publicly listed on the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Indonesian Stock Exchange">Indonesian Stock Exchange</a> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated45_99-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated45-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/KFC_in_Japan" title="KFC in Japan">KFC in Japan</a></div>
<p>KFC Japan was formed in 1970 as a <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint venture</a> between the American parent and the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Corporation" title="Mitsubishi Corporation">Mitsubishi Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mitsubishi_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mitsubishi-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In December 1974, KFC Japan began to promote fried chicken as a <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> meal.<sup id="cite_ref-mitsubishi2_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mitsubishi2-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Eating KFC as a Christmas time meal has since become a widely practiced custom in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-xmas_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xmas-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=KFC&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Japan is the third-largest market for KFC after China and the United States with 1,200 outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-yumstores_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yumstores-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2007, Mitsubishi assumed majority control of KFC Japan in a JP¥ 14.83 billion transaction.<sup id="cite_ref-jt_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jt-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg/220px-KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg/330px-KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg/440px-KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="735" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Cheesy_Potato_Wedges.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KFC <a href="/wiki/Cheddar_sauce" title="Cheddar sauce">Cheesy</a> <a href="/wiki/Potato_wedges" title="Potato wedges">Wedges</a>, available domestically only in the country. First introduced around 2005, it is one of the bestselling items in the Malaysian KFC.</div></div></div>
<p>Being one of its largest overseas markets, the Malaysian KFC traces its origin from  January 1, 1973 from its first outlet in <a href="/wiki/Jalan_Tunku_Abdul_Rahman" class="mw-redirect" title="Jalan Tunku Abdul Rahman">Jalan Tunku Abdul Rahman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dine_in_KFC_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dine_in_KFC-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the brand has been crowned as the largest fast-food chain in Malaysia and dominating 45% of the local Fast-Food Market shares with its traditional rival, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a> following in second, while its sister restaurant, <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a> spotting at the third place. By 2018, the restaurant has established a strong presence in the country, estimated to serve almost an equal proportion with the total population of Malaysia with 25 million customers every month by its 14,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-KFC_Malaysia_now_has_more_than_480_outlets_in_four_countries_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KFC_Malaysia_now_has_more_than_480_outlets_in_four_countries-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QSR_Brands_targets_RM5bil_revenue_this_year_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QSR_Brands_targets_RM5bil_revenue_this_year-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Rice_Set_(Malaysia)_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/KFC_Rice_Set_%28Malaysia%29_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg/220px-KFC_Rice_Set_%28Malaysia%29_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/KFC_Rice_Set_%28Malaysia%29_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg/330px-KFC_Rice_Set_%28Malaysia%29_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/KFC_Rice_Set_%28Malaysia%29_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg/440px-KFC_Rice_Set_%28Malaysia%29_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC_Rice_Set_(Malaysia)_and_Chicken_Nuggets.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2 pieces of "Hot &amp; Spicy" Chicken combo served with rice, <a href="/wiki/Coleslaw" title="Coleslaw">coleslaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_chili_sauce" title="Sweet chili sauce">Thai chili sauce</a>; with KFC Chicken nuggets with <a href="/wiki/Sour_cream" title="Sour cream">sour cream</a> sauce on the upper left side of the image. Akin to most Asian markets, the Malaysian KFC similarly offered rice in its menu. Embracing the local culinary tradition, the Malaysian KFC rice draw its inspiration from the local <a href="/wiki/Hainanese_chicken_rice" title="Hainanese chicken rice">Hainanese chicken rice</a>. Additionally, the KFC chicken nuggets also traced its origin from Malaysia before being expanded to many international outlets.</div></div></div>
<p>Similar to other international KFC markets, the Malaysian KFC also featuring various localised and seasonal food items in addition to the universal KFC Menu. The Malaysian KFC customarily offers two types of <a href="/wiki/Fried_chicken" title="Fried chicken">fried chicken</a>: Original and Hot &amp; Spicy, moreover, other types of fried chickens and food products are also being periodically introduced to the local consumers. Among other common year-long regional items unique to the Malaysian market includes <a href="/wiki/Hainanese_chicken_rice" title="Hainanese chicken rice">chicken rice</a>, rice <a href="/wiki/Congee" title="Congee">congee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrap_(food)" title="Wrap (food)">wrap</a>, cheesy <a href="/wiki/Potato_wedges" title="Potato wedges">potato wedges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gula_melaka" class="mw-redirect" title="Gula melaka">gula melaka</a> vanilla pudding, <a href="/wiki/White_coffee#Malaysia" title="White coffee">white coffee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teh_tarik" title="Teh tarik">teh tarik</a>. Malaysians mostly prefer <a href="/wiki/Dark_meat" class="mw-redirect" title="Dark meat">dark meat</a> cuts, a divergent from the American KFC that observed <a href="/wiki/White_meat" title="White meat">white meat</a> in a higher demand. Furthermore, being a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Islamic_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic country">Muslim-country</a>, all meats are slaughtered in accord to the <a href="/wiki/Halal" title="Halal">Halal</a>-method under the supervision of Shariah Advisory Council and the Department of Islamic Development Malaysia.
</p><p>The KFC business design in Malaysian is generally offering a mid-range dining option to cater the predominantly <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Malaysia" title="Economy of Malaysia">middle-class Malaysian</a> population. The premise is typically large in area and able to accommodate the dining culture commonly practised among the Malaysian society, a contrast to the primarily <a href="/wiki/Takeout" class="mw-redirect" title="Takeout">takeout</a> model seen in the American market. Many of the Malaysian KFC also operate <a href="/wiki/24/7_service" title="24/7 service">round the clock</a>, offering <a href="/wiki/Drive-through" title="Drive-through">drive-through</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_delivery" title="Food delivery">delivery service</a>.
</p><p>As of 2018, QSR Brands (M) Holdings Bhd, the shareholder of the company in Malaysia is also responsible on managing 810 KFC outlets across Malaysia, Singapore, Brunei and Cambodia,<sup id="cite_ref-QSR_Brands_Nak_Disenaraikan_Di_Bursa_Malaysia_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QSR_Brands_Nak_Disenaraikan_Di_Bursa_Malaysia-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> with more than 700 of these outlets are being located domestically in Malaysia, hence making the country one of the largest global market for the fast-food chain. The chain has been witnessed rapid expansion since the opening of its 250th Malaysian outlet on May 8, 1998 located in <a href="/wiki/Petronas_Twin_Towers" class="mw-redirect" title="Petronas Twin Towers">Petronas Twin Towers</a>, the 500th branch in <a href="/wiki/Subang,_Selangor" title="Subang, Selangor">Subang</a> launched on January 15, 2011 and the 700th restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Seremban" title="Seremban">Seremban</a> on September 18, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_Milestones_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our_Milestones-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dine_in_KFC_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dine_in_KFC-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Additionally, the QSR Brands is also in change on handling 380 <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a> outlets in Malaysia and 80 in Singapore, similar to some international developments, many of these restaurants are being traditionally combined together with a KFC premise. The company is estimated earn <a href="/wiki/Ringgit" class="mw-redirect" title="Ringgit">MYR</a>5 billion in revenue for KFC and Pizza Hut throughout the region in 2018, up from MYR4.56 billion (2017) and MYR4.24 billion (2016), the period recorded the company earned a profit of MYR182.98 million and MYR113.44 million in 2017 and 2016 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-QSR’s_return_to_the_stock_market_is_finally_happening_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QSR’s_return_to_the_stock_market_is_finally_happening-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dine_in_KFC_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dine_in_KFC-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1995, <i>Projek Penyayang</i> KFC was founded in an effort to provide food to more than 150 orphanages every quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-kfcmalaysia_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kfcmalaysia-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The social service by the restaurant was then extended by the introduction of <i>Tabung Penyayang</i> Fund in 1997, Add Hope Malaysia in 2006 and Add Hope Wordwide in 2007 as means to aid the local and international community.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_Community,_Our_Responsibility_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our_Community,_Our_Responsibility-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KFC_gives_back_to_society_via_Tabung_Penyayang_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KFC_gives_back_to_society_via_Tabung_Penyayang-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The chain is also one of the earliest fast-food eateries in Malaysia to employ people with <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">different abilities</a> from its outlet in <a href="/wiki/Jalan_Imbi" title="Jalan Imbi">Jalan Imbi</a>, Kuala Lumpur in November 15, 1986 (has since relocated to Sentul Raya, <a href="/wiki/Jalan_Ipoh" title="Jalan Ipoh">Jalan Ipoh</a> in 1992).<sup id="cite_ref-Disabled_shine_at_work_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disabled_shine_at_work-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KFC_outlet_with_a_difference_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KFC_outlet_with_a_difference-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
From the first fully operated KFC in the world run by speech-and hearing-impaired staff in Kuala Lumpur, the operation has expanded to its Malaysian operation in <a href="/wiki/Tanjung_Aru" title="Tanjung Aru">Tanjung Aru</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kota_Kinabalu" title="Kota Kinabalu">Kota Kinabalu</a>) and Saujana (<a href="/wiki/Kuching" title="Kuching">Kuching</a>) outlets in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Deaf_Kentucky_Fried_Chicken!_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deaf_Kentucky_Fried_Chicken!-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
Similarly, the model has also being adopted by several KFC eateries in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, India, Pakistan, Singapore and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>. To date, the establishment has employed more than 350 Malaysian individuals predominantly of speech and hearing impairment.
</p><p>KFC Malaysia is expected to have a 5% growth on sales in 2019. It has opened 23 outlets in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-KFC_Malaysia_plans_expansion_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KFC_Malaysia_plans_expansion-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KFC_targets_5_pc_growth_in_2019_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KFC_targets_5_pc_growth_in_2019-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> a further 36 outlets in 2019 and 30 eateries later in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-QSR_Brands_targets_RM5bil_revenue_this_year_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QSR_Brands_targets_RM5bil_revenue_this_year-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KFC_targets_5_pc_growth_in_2019_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KFC_targets_5_pc_growth_in_2019-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC,_Belfast,_June_2010.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/KFC%2C_Belfast%2C_June_2010.JPG/220px-KFC%2C_Belfast%2C_June_2010.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/KFC%2C_Belfast%2C_June_2010.JPG/330px-KFC%2C_Belfast%2C_June_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/KFC%2C_Belfast%2C_June_2010.JPG/440px-KFC%2C_Belfast%2C_June_2010.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KFC,_Belfast,_June_2010.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A KFC in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, Northern Ireland</div></div></div>
<p>As of December 2013, there were 784 KFC outlets in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-restcount_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-restcount-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> British turnover was around £684.5 million in 2013, according to Technomic.<sup id="cite_ref-kfcukbw_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kfcukbw-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> About 70 percent of outlets are run by franchisees, with the remainder company owned.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The company employs 24,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Around 400 sites are drive-through outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Average outlet turnover is between £1 and £1.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Annual sales amount to 60,000 <a href="/wiki/Metric_tonne" class="mw-redirect" title="Metric tonne">metric tonnes</a> of chicken, 60 percent of which is purchased from the four largest suppliers in the UK, including <a href="/wiki/Faccenda_Group" title="Faccenda Group">Faccenda Group</a><sup id="cite_ref-faccenda_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faccenda-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2_Sisters_Food_Group" title="2 Sisters Food Group">2 Sisters Food Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> and delivered fresh to outlets at least three times a week.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoFE-40_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoFE-40-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The remaining 40 percent is sourced from companies in Europe, Thailand (including <a href="/wiki/Charoen_Pokphand_Foods" title="Charoen Pokphand Foods">Charoen Pokphand Foods</a>) and Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated18_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated18-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> All of the Original Recipe chicken is sourced within the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated18_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated18-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>England had the first overseas branch of KFC which opened in <a href="/wiki/Preston,_Lancashire" title="Preston, Lancashire">Preston</a>, Lancashire in May 1965, and was the first American fast food restaurant chain in the country, pre-dating the arrival of McDonald's, Burger King and <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a> by almost a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoFE-37_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoFE-37-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Ray Allen, an experienced Lancashire caterer, was the first franchisee.<sup id="cite_ref-lep_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lep-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The first London branch opened in <a href="/wiki/North_Finchley" title="North Finchley">North Finchley</a> in November 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-londonkfc_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-londonkfc-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In 1971 there were 31 outlets; by 1975 the chain had grown to 250 outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-nov75_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nov75-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1970s and throughout the 1980s, KFCs began to introduce seating. KFC opened its first drive through restaurant in the UK in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> By 1987 the company had almost 400 outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-JacobsScholliers2003_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JacobsScholliers2003-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 1997, the "Tower Burger", a fried chicken fillet sandwich with the addition of a <a href="/wiki/Hash_brown" class="mw-redirect" title="Hash brown">hash brown</a>, was first launched in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, the company stopped pre-salting its fries and removed trans fats from its products.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 palm oil was replaced by rapeseed oil in the fryers.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Between 2004 and 2014, KFC UK increased its offering of "portable" foods: sandwiches, wraps and salads.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> During that period, sales rose from around £500 million to almost £1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, KFC UK invested £9 million to install ovens in all of its outlets, so that it could offer griddled chicken.<sup id="cite_ref-shukerinterview2014_120-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shukerinterview2014-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, KFC rolled out <a href="/wiki/Lavazza" title="Lavazza">Lavazza</a> coffee across all of its UK outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-lavazza_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lavazza-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018, KFC had to temporarily close 575 of its UK outlets, and restrict menus and opening hours in other branches, as a result of its newly-contracted distributor, <a href="/wiki/DHL_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="DHL Express">DHL</a>, failing to deliver chicken to the outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> As of February 2019, KFC in the UK has around 110 restaurants that are Halal approved out of more than 900 units.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg/200px-Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg/300px-Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg/400px-Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kfc_in_Izmir.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A KFC in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a>, Turkey</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span></h4>
<p>KFC is planning on opening up to 50 franchise restaurants in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">Middle East</span></h3>
<p>The first KFC in the Middle East opened in 1973 in <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>. Today there are over 700 outlets, certified <a href="/wiki/Halal" title="Halal">halal</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan">Iraqi Kurdistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/KFC_Israel" title="KFC Israel">KFC Israel</a> existed from 1993 to 2013 and featured <a href="/wiki/Kashrut" title="Kashrut">kosher</a> restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 KFC opened in <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> in the Palestinian Authority<sup><a href="/wiki/KFC_Israel" title="KFC Israel">[8]</a></sup> and later expanded to Hebron,<sup><a href="/wiki/KFC_Israel" title="KFC Israel">[9]</a></sup> Bethlehem,<sup><a href="/wiki/KFC_Israel" title="KFC Israel">[10]</a></sup> Jenin,<sup><a href="/wiki/KFC_Israel" title="KFC Israel">[11]</a></sup> and three separate outlets in Ramallah: the Ersal Branch (Bacri), Plaza Mall Branch and Masyoun Branch.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 the New York Times reported that KFC was being smuggled into Gaza through tunnels.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span></h3>
